  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3c644a45-7120-4238-9bda-bdb50bbb5db8'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText7828079187757704463" style="display:none">After surviving a disastrous battle at prom, Alyssa has embraced her madness and gained perspective. She's determined to rescue her two worlds and the people and netherlings she loves. Even if it means challenging Queen Red to a final battle of wills and wiles . . . and even if the only way to Wonderland, now that the rabbit hole is closed, is through the looking-glass world--a parallel dimension filled with mutated and violent netherling outcasts. In the final installment of the wildly popular Splintered trilogy, Alyssa and her dad journey into the heart of magic and mayhem in search of her mom and to set right all that's gone wrong. Together with Jeb and Morpheus, they must salvage Wonderland from the decay and destruction that has ensnared it. But if they succeed and come out alive, can everyone truly have their happily ever after?</span>

Lol, I'm not about to try to change your mind, but my God what kind of inane drivel was that, hey?<br />Tbph I couldn't even go through with this one. I expect better from female authors. They degrade female protagonists in every possible way. God forbid we could have a heroine who is capable of wiping her own ar**.<br />If you want an uplifting and inspiring female lead I suggest you grab a Garth Nix or Jonathan Stroud book.<br />This trilogy read like the fantasy of a depraved, prematurely senile author clinging to the 'good old days' when women were creatures to be bedded and kept like pets . smh<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_884918824" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/884918824" />
    <a title="A.G. Howard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5920436-a-g-howard"><img alt="A.G. Howard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566101899p2/5920436.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/884918824?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="A.G. Howard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="A.G. Howard" href="/user/show/5920436-a-g-howard">A.G. Howard</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span> (Review from the author)


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer884918824" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17814137296000215740">Finished writing it! *blots sweat from brow* <br/><br/>Fair warning: Alyssa is a bit mad in this one. But she needs to be to get things done. Also, some VERY creepy critters and strange landscapes. And the boys? *LE SIGHS* the boys... <3 <br/><br/>****COVER UPDATE****<br/><br/>Okay, so the cover is live, and here are my thoughts on it: <br/><br/><a href='http://s1116.photobucket.com/user/aghoward6970/media/Ensnaredthoughts_zpsfbd21360.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1401291786i/9781383.jpg' alt='Ensnared thought cloud photo Ensnaredthoughts_zpsfbd21360.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Yes, there's a reason Jeb has a sexy harlequin vibe. <div id="review_858072551" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/858072551" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/858072551?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=dishonor-on-your-cow">dishonor-on-your-cow</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=protagonists-i-want-to-laser-face">protagonists-i-want-to-laser-face</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=bye-bye-nineteenth-amendment">bye-bye-nineteenth-amendment</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=surf-n-turf">surf-n-turf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=possible-creepers">possible-creepers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=i-spy-something-pointy">i-spy-something-pointy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=what-the-hell-was-that-endings">what-the-hell-was-that-endings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer858072551" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6861547726552816142"><blockquote>
  <i>"Please look at me. I missed you. I was so worried about you."<br/><br/>"Really? Which one of us are you talking to?"</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>If you recall, I'd caved and read the epilogue for Ensnared first, which led to me punching the wall in anger and spent the rest of the afternoon ranting my poor sister's ear off. <br/><br/>Well, I'm here to tell you I read the rest of it. Aaaand I'm still infuriated.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427119720ra/14237658.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I just have more leverage.<br/><br/>Ensnared puts forth the conundrum of Al being torn between her human and Netherling sides, more specifica</span>
  <span id="freeText6861547726552816142" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"Please look at me. I missed you. I was so worried about you."<br><br>"Really? Which one of us are you talking to?"</i>
</blockquote><br><br>If you recall, I'd caved and read the epilogue for Ensnared first, which led to me punching the wall in anger and spent the rest of the afternoon ranting my poor sister's ear off. <br><br>Well, I'm here to tell you I read the rest of it. Aaaand I'm still infuriated.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427119720ra/14237658.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I just have more leverage.<br><br>Ensnared puts forth the conundrum of Al being torn between her human and Netherling sides, more specifically, two hot, perfect guys. <br><br>Let's take a look-see at our contestants, shall we?<br><br>First up, <b>Jeb</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"I'll decide how much she needs to know and when to tell her."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Yes, this dreamy human hunk likes to speak caveman and treat our fretting heroine like a glass figurine. He's such a supporter of women's rights, he decides to win Al's heart by <b>asking her father, instead of her personally, for her hand.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"He was planning to ask you to marry him. Did you know that? He asked me for your hand."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Because he recognizes the ancient law of male ownership over women, he doesn't ask for Daddy's <i>blessing</i>, but his <i>permission</i>. <br><br>He is also a master of <b>emotional manipulation</b>. Sensing Al's guilt in kissing Hot Guy #2 and accidentally sending him to Wonderland last book, he strong-arms Al into making a life-magic vow that gives him first dibs on everything. Marriage, virginity, children, oral sex... you name it. If she breaks it, she'll lose her magic and possibly doom Wonderland for all eternity.<br><br>Hear that, girls? He wants to be your first or no deal. Don't everybody rush him at once.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427119720i/14237659.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In the other corner, we have <b>Morpheus.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"The way he shoves me into the face of danger, forces me to look beyond my fears and reach for my full potential."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>This winged Netherling is manipulative, strategic (though Jeb could give him a run for his money!) and smells like tobacco, probably encouraging impressible young tweens everywhere to smoke in hopes it'll land them their dream girl/boy. <br><br>No matter what, he'll always put Wonderland first. Unless it comes to his queen, Al, who also happens to be the only one able to save Wonderland! What a coincidink!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427119720ra/14237660.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Who can forget the lady of the hour, <b>Al</b>!<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"In the darkness, beneath the covers, I hug myself tight, surrounded by Jeb's scent and Morpheus's homespun lingerie."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Descendent of the Red Queen, Al is half-human, half-Netherling and gifted with tremendous magic. In her quest to save Wonderland, she will openly toy with both boys' affections, scold herself for being selfish, then keep on doing it anyway! <br><br>They are literally two halves of her heart and for some inexplicable reason, <b>she needs men to realize her potential.</b> Jeb championing her human side, Morpheus the Netherling. Because <b>sixteen years of being a human is not enough</b> to sustain the former.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427119720ra/14237661.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Here are your contestants and here are your <b>Possible endings:</b><br><br><u>Ending A:</u> Al ends up with Morpheus, Jeb having died in a hole somewhere. Morpheus educates her in the ways of madness, and Al uses her sixteen years of humanity to retain herself. <br><br><u>Ending B:</u> Morpheus dies, and his magic fuses with Jeb, like in Elsewhere (Morpheus couldn't use magic there and channeled it into Jeb, like a vessel). Al helps him control his darker side or he puts on his big-boy pants and does it himself, relying on sixteen years of experience. They smooch and rule side by side in Wonderland.<br><br><u>Ending C:</u> Al punts both boys on their ass and rules Wonderland on her own. (Personally, I'm rooting for this one)<br><br><u>Ending D:</u> Al sacrifices herself for Wonderland. Jeb and Morpheus finally give in to their latent homosexual desire for each other and become the first same-sex reigning couple in Wonderland.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"'How does [Morpheus] know your measurements, huh?'<br><br>I frown and drop my arm. 'I could ask the same thing about your boxers. You can't even sew a button onto a shirt.'"</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427119720ra/14237662.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Guess which ending Ensnared went with?<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><blockquote><i>"So, after everyone dies, you'll go to Wonderland and be perpetually sixteen?"</i></blockquote>
<br><br>After they defeat Red, both boys accept they have to be constants in Al's life. She lives out her human life with Jeb, prepping with Morpheus by night, and after he kicks the bucket, she rejoins Hot Guy #2 in Wonderland. Youth magically restored, Al is crowned queen and lives happily ever after with Morpheus. How's that for a have-your-cake-and-eat-it-too situation?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422767372ra/13543456.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422767372ra/13543457.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422767372ra/13543458.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Al gets fucking <i>everything</i>—youth, power, both men—and doesn't have to lift a damn finger. Jeb and Morpheus are the ones who had to make hard choices, to compromise, to give up shit. <br><br>The book attempts to fool us into thinking Al has to abandon her family and it's all so sad and self-sacrificing. Fuck that. She's a freaking magic queen! She can glamor a disguise and see them whenever she wants. If she's feeling particularly selfish, which isn't hard, she can spirit them to Wonderland and everyone can have Sunday dinner together like one, big happy family. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421416113i/13373303._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I awarded it an extra star for the writing world-building, which is glorious.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"One creature is a pale, cone-headed humanoid whose cranium pops open sporadically so she can argue with a smaller version of herself. Next, the smaller version's cranium opens to reveal an even littler likeness. The tiniest one is a male with a large nose. He bonks his female counterparts with a rolling pin before hiding away again."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Shame the characters suck.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/852434557" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of Splintered</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/858062116" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of Unhinged</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1223504075" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of Untamed</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="6861547726552816142" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer705468685" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9571830839986722138"><a href='http://socially-awkward-bookworm.tumblr.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409761094i/11018340.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/></a><br/><br/><i>WARNING: Since this is the final book of a trilogy this review will have slight spoilers for book one and two.</i><br/><br/><b>Synopsis</b><br/><br/>Alyssa is on a mission to not only save Morpheus and Jeb from the twisted looking glass world of AnyElsewhere, but she also needs to save all of Wonderland and her mother. The only way to save everyone will be to embrace the netherling madness within her and defeat Queen Red once and for all. With the help of her father, Alyssa ventures through the looking glass to set things ri</span>
  <span id="freeText9571830839986722138" style="display:none"><a href="http://socially-awkward-bookworm.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409761094i/11018340.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br><i>WARNING: Since this is the final book of a trilogy this review will have slight spoilers for book one and two.</i><br><br><b>Synopsis</b><br><br>Alyssa is on a mission to not only save Morpheus and Jeb from the twisted looking glass world of AnyElsewhere, but she also needs to save all of Wonderland and her mother. The only way to save everyone will be to embrace the netherling madness within her and defeat Queen Red once and for all. With the help of her father, Alyssa ventures through the looking glass to set things right. But even if she can save everyone and fix the damage done by Queen Red, will she ever truly be able to live happily ever after being torn between the two different sides of herself?<br><br><b>Thoughts</b><br><br>Returning to this series for the final book is bittersweet. It was like curling up with an old favorite, even though I had never read it before. But it was the end, so it was like saying goodbye to a best friend. There’s just something about Anita’s darker take on Wonderland that draws me in and doesn’t let me go. I’m not usually one to get a book hangover, but with this series every book made it difficult to move on. And now we’ve come to the final book.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422471060ra/13504603.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Even though I hate seeing this series come to an end, I am in love with how this series wraps up. While Alyssa is still torn between her human and netherling sides, she’s definitely more willing to give into her Wonderland side to get things done. She is one kickass heroine. My love for Morpheus once again knows no bounds, manipulative bastard that he is, and even Jeb has some redeeming qualities. I’m not usually one for love triangles, but this one…<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422471060ra/13504604.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>While the love triangle does play an integral part in the story, there is SO much more. AnyElsewhere is a whole different kind of twisted than Wonderland. There are plenty of more fantastical creatures to be seen, adventures to be had, and outcomes to be manipulated. <br><br>I picked up Splintered way back in 2013 when I was in search for a stand alone, but I’m so glad that we were given a deeper look into the mad and wonderfully twisted worlds of Wonderland and AnyElsewhere. I can’t recall ever giving all the books in a series 5 stars, but this one was a perfect fit for me. I foresee myself revisiting many times in the future and look forward to, hopefully, many more books from Anita.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380428023ra/855984.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Me before the book published: It's going to be a trilogy?!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380434597ra/877306.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I cannot contain my excitment!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380434597ra/877307.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>B-But I have to wait till 2015?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380434597ra/877308.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="9571830839986722138" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_712133493" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/712133493" />
    <a title="Teresa Mary Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6054096-teresa-mary-rose"><img alt="Teresa Mary Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579051556p2/6054096.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/712133493?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Teresa Mary Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Teresa Mary Rose" href="/user/show/6054096-teresa-mary-rose">Teresa Mary Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/24356258-ensnared">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6054096-teresa-mary-rose?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6054096-teresa-mary-rose?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6054096-teresa-mary-rose?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6054096-teresa-mary-rose?shelf=cover-love">cover-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6054096-teresa-mary-rose?shelf=re-readable-books">re-readable-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6054096-teresa-mary-rose?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer712133493" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9003301604448761346">More Reviews Here: <a href='http://readerslive1000lives.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Readers Live A Thousand Lives</a><br/><br/>I was wary going into Ensnared. I have absolutely loved this series but Ensnared got some very very mixed reviews, so I didn’t know what side of the fence I was going to fall on. That’s probably part of the reason I didn’t read it immediately; I think I needed to distance myself from all of the talk. I’m glad I waited to read this one because I ended up enjoying it a lot. Ensnared wasn’t my favorite of the series but I did think it was a great read</span>
  <span id="freeText9003301604448761346" style="display:none">More Reviews Here: <a href="http://readerslive1000lives.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Readers Live A Thousand Lives</a><br /><br />I was wary going into Ensnared. I have absolutely loved this series but Ensnared got some very very mixed reviews, so I didn’t know what side of the fence I was going to fall on. That’s probably part of the reason I didn’t read it immediately; I think I needed to distance myself from all of the talk. I’m glad I waited to read this one because I ended up enjoying it a lot. Ensnared wasn’t my favorite of the series but I did think it was a great read and a solid conclusion.<br /><br />I really love Alyssa as a heroine. I love how strong she is and that she is so determined. She has finally come to terms with both sides of herself and acknowledges that she can love both of those sides and embrace them. She isn’t one to sit on the sidelines. She is always right in the middle of the action and is usually the strongest player in the game.<br /><br />Then there is Jeb and Morpheus and I’ve always said this is one of my very favorite love triangles. I genuinely like both guys even when they each have their moments. It’s no secret I’m 100% Team Morpheus because I prefer him, but I don’t and can’t hate Jeb. It’s clear that they both love Alyssa and it’s clear that she loves them both. It really is an agonizing choice and neither choice is wrong. Jeb brings out her humanity and compassion while Morpheus pushes and challenges her to be the best she can. My heart was breaking right alongside Alyssa in this one. I will forever contend though that Morpheus understood Alyssa in a way nobody else could and respected her and knew she was strong.<br /><br />Once again I loved the world A.G. Howard has created. Anyelsewhere is creepy and demented and crazy. And of course I adore this version of Wonderland. The world building is just fantastic.<br /><br />All in all, I really enjoyed Ensnared and I’m happy with the way everything wrapped up. This series remains one of my favorites and I look forward to revisiting it again one day.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9003301604448761346" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer804797328" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer18314373894483599113">I'm still not anywhere near to writing a proper review for this book. It's been 5 months now and I'm still a mess of emotions. I swear, I've developed a split personality disorder with the ending we got. Someone compared this feeling to a vortex in their review, and I couldn't agree more. I feel like I'll be forever swimming in this vortex. <br/><br/>On some days I'd feel *almost* okay about stuff, thanks to a few people who basically glued me back together again. I won't say the names, but you know who y</span>
  <span id="freeText18314373894483599113" style="display:none">I'm still not anywhere near to writing a proper review for this book. It's been 5 months now and I'm still a mess of emotions. I swear, I've developed a split personality disorder with the ending we got. Someone compared this feeling to a vortex in their review, and I couldn't agree more. I feel like I'll be forever swimming in this vortex. <br><br>On some days I'd feel *almost* okay about stuff, thanks to a few people who basically glued me back together again. I won't say the names, but you know who you are. Thank you all for your eternal patience. (@Nessy, I know you are reading this, and if you are wondering, yes, you are one of those people. I mean, you dedicated your whole review to me, so I had to let you know. :P)<br><br>If I squint out of the corner of my eye, the ending almost makes sense to the story. Almost. If you don't think too much about how it all really went on and the implications. Yes, if I try hard enough, I can find excuses and reasons for almost anything. I invented a whole lot of explanations why I supposedly understand this, and maybe I'll write them down here some day, so you guys see how a tired mind can justify anything, just to stop hurting, just so I could move on to happier thoughts.<br><br>But every once in a while I would see someone's update, or read a review that resonated too deeply with my own feelings, and I would understand how flimsy the peace I made with the ending is. I don't know what it would take to get over all this. Read Untamed, maybe?<br><br>***<br><br>I have trouble dealing with the resolution of this series. <br>But I'm sure most people will like how it ended, so don't let my personal feelings discourage you. It was poignant and beautiful and funny and painful at the same time.<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420704516i/13253865.jpg" width="320" height="236" alt="tears" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br></span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2263166738" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2263166738" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45261627-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475352701p2/45261627.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2263166738?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/45261627-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=because-bad-boys">because-bad-boys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=kings-and-queens">kings-and-queens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=was-that-really-necessary">was-that-really-necessary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=beware-of-love-triangle">beware-of-love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=hooray-for-innuendo">hooray-for-innuendo</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=heartthrobs-and-heroes">heartthrobs-and-heroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=unpopular-opinions">unpopular-opinions</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=published-fanfiction">published-fanfiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2263166738" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13722147185658517819">The first fifty or so pages of <i>Ensnared</i>, the conclusion to A.G. Howard’s Splintered trilogy, are a solid adventure story as Alyssa and her father search for an entrance to Wonderland and the adjoining dark realm of AnyElsewhere, where evil Queen Red dragged Morpheus, Allison, and Jeb at the end of <i>Unhinged</i>. <br/><br/>We’re learning all kinds of stuff about Alyssa’s dad, who had no memories of life before Pleasance, TX, until recently, and whose whole identity was assigned by Allison years ago. His name is</span>
  <span id="freeText13722147185658517819" style="display:none">The first fifty or so pages of <i>Ensnared</i>, the conclusion to A.G. Howard’s Splintered trilogy, are a solid adventure story as Alyssa and her father search for an entrance to Wonderland and the adjoining dark realm of AnyElsewhere, where evil Queen Red dragged Morpheus, Allison, and Jeb at the end of <i>Unhinged</i>. <br><br>We’re learning all kinds of stuff about Alyssa’s dad, who had no memories of life before Pleasance, TX, until recently, and whose whole identity was assigned by Allison years ago. His name is really David Skeffington (arguably the most English name ever), not Thomas Gardner, and he’s not only English, but part of a knightly bloodline sworn to protect the gates between the worlds.<br><br>This is a lot of information to digest, but it’s so exciting that I scarcely cared. The parents in YA books are overwhelmingly useless , and I <b>
  <i>LOVE</i>
</b> how Howard has made not just one of the MC’s parents empowered and central to the plot, but <i>both</i>. <br><br>When they reach AnyElsewhere they meet up with Morpheus to save Wonderland—<br><br>And then Jeb happened. *sad trombone*<br><br><b>Content Advisory</b><br><i>Violence</i>: Lots of surreal violence—human vs. humanoid, human vs. monster, two souls fighting each other for control of a single body. A lot of this also goes under <i>Nightmare Fuel</i>.<br><br><i>Sex</i>: A LOT of goofy make-out scenes. The Morpheus/Alyssa ones were bearable. The Jeb/Al ones, on the other hand, were devoid of spark and frankly abhorrent. Also they were in their undergarments one time for no reason. This shows how desperate Howard was to sell us Jeb-as-love-interest—Jeb in his boxers is meh, Morpheus in a full three-piece suit can start a forest fire just by blinking. Not recommended for the under 14 crowd. The Y in YA stands for <i>young</i>, people.<br><br>As always, Morpheus makes innuendos. They’re about as raunchy as those of Hawkeye Pierce on <i>M*A*S*H</i>, a phrase which here means “not all that raunchy.” Also, he hears Alyssa complaining about her ugly asylum issue undergarments, <i>sews her some pretty silk lingerie, and <b>leaves it on her pillow</b></i>. It’s sweet that he paid so much attention to her wants, and I applaud his craftiness—nothing manlier than a guy who’s not afraid to sew, cook, or do other “chick” things—but dude, you’re not even dating yet. That’s kind of creepy.<br><br>At one point everyone’s outer clothes get destroyed and Jeb has to paint them on. A dumb excuse for showing skin and Jeb being “useful.”<br><br><i>Language</i>: Morpheus’ favorite word, after “luv,” is still “bloody.”<br><br><i>Substance Abuse</i>: I got nothin’.<br><br><i>Nightmare Fuel</i>: 80% of the book is this. Jeb created an evil doppelganger who has gaping holes in his body and wants to kill everyone. Morpheus almost gets dismembered and eaten by gorilla-kingfisher mutants. There are land-dwelling flying piranhas that eat people and animals alive. A guy gets his eyes gauged out and tongue chopped off (not shown). Both Red and Hart possess Alyssa’s body like demons at one point. Since the Queen of Hearts is a character here, decapitation is a constant threat for all. And I’m sure I’m forgetting stuff. <br><br>Yeah, don’t read this book late at night.<br><br><b>The Problem of Jeb</b><br>Howard’s world-building is a beautiful, earnest tribute to Carroll while being innovative and rich in its own right. She cleverly references her source material and other works. Alyssa and her parents can be (and usually are) pig-headed idiots, but our heroine is somewhat developed, and the parents defy expectations. Morpheus is a magnificent anti-hero on par with Erik the Opera Ghost, Howl Jenkins, Jareth the Goblin King, Eugenides, Han Solo and his son Ben. <br><br>But Jeb…Jeb is a black hole where a character should be. He’s a splicing of Anakin Skywalker and Frank Burns, and just as charming as that implies. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1525102007ra/25458336.gif" width="500" height="206" alt="Anakin AotC" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1525102007ra/25458332.gif" width="245" height="163" alt="Frank" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Remove the make-out scenes and Jeb spends two books tagging along and getting captured. Nothing that a younger sibling or younger sibling-like character couldn’t do. He could be Toby from <i>Labyrinth</i> or Wentworth from <i>The Wee Free Men</i>. Jeb does some nice things in this last book, but they’re way out of character (as my friend Nicki pointed out in her review) and far too late. His back-story is sad, but he’s so obnoxious that I don’t care. He will never be one-quarter the man that Morpheus is.<br><br>But not only does Howard apparently want us to <i>like</i> Jeb, she forces Alyssa’s parents to love Jeb, even though he has done nothing to earn their love, and hate and mistrust Morpheus, even though he has done nothing but help them for years, putting up with all manner of abuse in the meanwhile. Alyssa, at least, is seventeen and has an excuse to be stupid. <br><br>This love triangle could even work if Jeb were a consistent character and contrasted in a meaningful way with Morpheus. Let’s look at <i>The Phantom of the Opera</i>. Christine Daeë, our heroine, is about the same age as Alyssa and just as confused. She has two suitors: one is Erik Destler(?), the dangerous magician who (in the Lloyd-Webber version at least) loves her for her talent as well as her beauty, and empathizes with her because she’s almost as isolated as he is. The other is Raoul de Chagny, the wealthy and sanguine youth who likes Christine’s pretty face, has been comfortable and popular his whole life, is kind of shallow, and is just the sort of boy that parents approve of.<br><br>While most readers/viewers wanted Christine to pick Erik, it makes sense that she would cling to Raoul. She’s just a kid and he’s <i>safe</i>. Erik is much better suited for her, but he means adulthood in all its aspects—power, responsibility, sexuality, moral ambiguity, and ultimately death. Raoul, being made of sunshine and cinnamon and frolicking puppies, represents a postponement of all that. Granted, Erik kind of shot himself in the foot. He had a real knack for impulsively strangling folks and dropping chandeliers and getting angry mobs after him. <br><br>Christine herself represents feminine energy, resurrection, redemption, and the promise of new life. <br><br>In Splintered, we have our embodiment of Scary Adult Things in Morpheus, who, like Erik, is a literary descendant of Hades. We have our Creative Potential/Fertility/Death and Resurrection/Redemptrix figure in Alyssa, who like Christine, is a modernized Persephone. And Jeb has no place in the archetype because he’s not like Raoul. He’s not wholesome, cheery or sweet, and the last thing on his mind is guarding Alyssa’s innocence. <br><br>So there’s no reason for him to be here. He should either have a)replaced with a wholesome boy, b) been demoted to kid brother/platonic friend, or c) written out altogether. <br><br><b>The Ivory Gate</b><br>In the <i>Aeneid</i>, Virgil claims that there are two exits from the Underworld:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>There are two gates of Sleep, one said to be<br>Of horn, whereby the true shades pass with ease,<br>The other all white ivory agleam<br>Without a flaw, and yet false dreams are sent <br>Through this one by the ghosts to the upper world.<br>Anchises now, his last instructions given,<br>Took [Aeneas] and [the] Sibyl there and let them go<br>By the Ivory Gate.</i>
</blockquote><br>~<i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12914.The_Aeneid" title="The Aeneid by Virgil" rel="nofollow noopener">The Aeneid</a>
</i>, Book VI, verses 1212 – 1218 (Robert Fitzgerald translation)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525102007i/25458334._SX540_.jpg" width="660" height="419" alt="Aeneas' descendants" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This passage stood out to me when I read the poem for English class. Further research brought up many different interpretations. Some scholars argue that it only refers to what time of day Aeneas reemerged. Others speculate that it’s an early example of metafiction—or it signifies that everything Aeneas does from Book VII onward is somehow…false. Like he and the Sibyl reemerged in a parallel universe, a dream very like reality but not exactly right. It would explain why the poem becomes 50% more surreal after this point, events moving with dreamlike speed and personalities changing like nightmares. <br><br>One of my teachers theorized that Virgil didn’t really believe Aeneas was a hero, and that this passage was the first clue. If he were really a good guy, my teacher argued, he would have been able to pass by the Horn Gate. As it is, he and the Sibyl had to reenter the living world as lies, as fictions of themselves. The teacher felt that the end of the poem, where Aeneas abandons his principles and stabs an enemy begging for mercy, proved that this Aeneas is not the same Aeneas who entered the Land of the Dead.<br><br>Long before Alice fell down a hole and found a strange world below, Persephone did. I discussed earlier how Morpheus and Alyssa are a variation on Hades and Persephone—he rules an underground realm and can be invisible/a moth when he wishes, she enters his domain and lives to tell about it and also has a connection with plants. Jeb, according to this scheme, is the mortal Pirithous, who in his hubris thought he could carry off Persephone. (Persephone was a lot smarter than Alyssa and paid him no mind).<br><br>But the mythical stuff goes further than that. The first 50 or so pages of this very book are all about <i>gates</i> between the real world and various topsy-turvy-lands…the sort of places one could only access by, say, an ivory gate. And there is even a character named Ivory here. Also, like Aeneas, Alyssa is granted a vision of her descendants. It motivated Aeneas to find Lavinia and bring Silvius into the world, but Alyssa is happy to put her Child of Destiny with Morpheus on hold until she’s produced an unnecessary family with Jeb. Morpheus is both Hades and Lavinia (a zany combination of mythological figures if ever there was one), Alyssa is Persephone/Aeneas, and that makes Jeb not just Pirithous but Dido. <i>Let him GO</i>, Al.<br><br>Earlier I was complaining that Jeb really drags this series down, and would need to either not exist at all or be a very different character in order not to. But even his continued, obnoxious, unchanged existence I could tolerate if only it had ended differently.<br><br>Because Alyssa rashly makes an unbreakable magic vow to Jeb that he will be her first husband, and she will return to Texas as soon as possible to grow old at his side. Everything her real country needs from her—such as her being Queen and bringing them an heir with both human and Netherling powers—can wait fifty or sixty years. How very selfless of her.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525102007i/25458337.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="Grumpy Cat No" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>From here on out, the characters sally forth from the Ivory Gate, for this is not where the story’s supposed to go. To be a hero, Alyssa would have to <i>grow up</i> and put aside childish things. Jeb, for all his forced sexual energy, is a childish thing as far as Al’s concerned. She’s known him as long as she can remember, and now she’s being called to rule a world that he can’t even survive long in. She has to release him. Either that or make the wrong choice, go back with him and her parents and forget Morpheus and Wonderland.<br><br>This is not an attack on Howard. Plenty of wonderful authors have done this—Jane Austen, L.M. Montgomery, J.K. Rowling and Rick Riordan among them. Austen forced the character Henry Crawford to commit an over-the-top act of immorality just when he was starting to redeem himself, her logic being that she didn’t want <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45032.Mansfield_Park" title="Mansfield Park by Jane Austen" rel="nofollow noopener">Mansfield Park</a>
</i> to be a repeat of <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1885.Pride_and_Prejudice" title="Pride and Prejudice by Jane Austen" rel="nofollow noopener">Pride and Prejudice</a>
</i> (Jane’s sister Cassandra was displeased with this development). Montgomery destroyed the character of Dean Priest because he was based on her husband, and she wanted to pair the autobiographical Emily Starr off with Teddy Kent, a.k.a. “the one who got away.” Rowling started out intending to redeem Draco Malfoy, even making him a valued friend to Harry and Hermione’s love interest, but scrapped this because children needed to learn that people can’t change and forgiveness is for losers or something. Riordan set up a love triangle between Luke Castellan, Annabeth Chase, and Percy Jackson, which he solved by forcing Annabeth to friendzone Luke while he died in her arms. Boo.<br><br>Let me clarify: the way the story should go ≠ the way I personally want it to go. I didn’t want Frodo and the Elves to leave Middle-earth at the end of <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18512.The_Return_of_the_King__The_Lord_of_the_Rings___3_" title="The Return of the King (The Lord of the Rings, #3) by J.R.R. Tolkien" rel="nofollow noopener">The Return of the King</a>
</i>, and I certainly didn’t want Beth to die in <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1934.Little_Women__Little_Women___1_" title="Little Women (Little Women, #1) by Louisa May Alcott" rel="nofollow noopener">Little Women</a>
</i>. But every good story has loss…<br><br><b>This is a Gift, It Comes with a Price</b><br>*hat tip to Florence + the Machine*<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1525102007ra/25458335.gif" width="500" height="273" alt="Florence" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When Alyssa saw her future son in <i>Unhinged</i>, I immediately thought of the scene in the film version of <i>The Return of the King</i> where Arwen sees <i>her</i> future son and decides to stay in Middle-earth. Staying meant that she’d never see her family again this side of the far green country. Aragorn would age and die, but she would not. Her children would also age and die, and she would linger as some kind of shade, only dying after many long years.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1516714802ra/24900927.gif" width="356" height="200" alt="Arwen's vision" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Some might argue that Alyssa makes the same choice as Arwen, but Alyssa actually makes the opposite choice. Arwen’s was a sacrifice. She got to stay with her beloved Aragorn, but at the cost of her immortality and her entire people. She gave up the familiar and comforting to stay in a changing world hemorrhaging of magic, and help her husband and friends keep it in order. She became deeply acquainted with grief. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1525102007ra/25458333.gif" width="245" height="163" alt="Aragorn's grave" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Alyssa, on the other hand, gets to have a perfect human life with Jeb (*gags*), then as soon as he dies she hops back down the Rabbit Hole, becomes sixteen years old again, and becomes Morpheus’ merry queen forever more. This was dumb in <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1124884.The_Hero_and_the_Crown__Damar__1_" title="The Hero and the Crown (Damar #1) by Robin McKinley" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hero and the Crown</a>
</i>, too, but at least Aerin made sacrifices and felt obligated to marry Tor for the sake of Damar. Also Tor wasn't a jerk.<br><br>A quickie list of Other Fantasy Characters Who Sacrificed Things Because That’s How Fantasy Works:<br><br>•	In addition to Arwen, nearly every major character in LOTR gives things up. Frodo loses a finger, goes home traumatized, and eventually has to leave Middle-earth. Galadriel and Gandalf refuse the One Ring, lose the power in their own rings, and sail away with Frodo after becoming obsolete. Elrond gives up not just his ring and his kingdom, but his daughter. Faramir cedes the throne of Gondor to Aragorn. Everyone is willing to die so Frodo and Sam can accomplish their mission, which those two know they will not return from. <br><br>•	Luke Skywalker defeats the Empire and redeems his father, only for his father to promptly die on him. By then he has also lost both his mentors, the aunt and uncle who raised him, and his hand. <br><br>•	Another member of the One-Handed Hero Club is <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Eugenides of Eddis, who sacrificed his right hand, his health and his family to wed his beloved Irene and unite his home peninsula against invaders. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>•	Yet another member of the OHHC is <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Lirael of the Clayr, who defeats an existential threat to the universe but loses her hand and her guardian angel doggy. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>•	Alanna of Trebond <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[saves her kingdom from an evil usurper, but loses her twin brother, one of her boyfriends, and her guardian angel kitty. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Interestingly, the two young men in <i>Ensnared</i> sacrifice a great deal. Morpheus has always relied on his magic. For the bulk of this book, he is stripped of his powers and has to rely on the person he hates most for survival. Jeb’s willingness to surrender is way out of character, but credit where credit is due. He also knows what his wife will do when he dies and marries her anyway.<br><br>But Alyssa gets everything on her own terms. She wanted <i>both</i>, both boys, both lives, and she got them. She’s not a hero like Arwen, Frodo, Luke, etc. She didn’t learn a blessed thing. This beautifully-written series could have closed with a powerful message about coming of age. Instead it goes out with the whimper of teenage wish fulfillment. What a missed opportunity.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="13722147185658517819" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Liz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14811808-liz"><img alt="Liz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585394064p2/14811808.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/856701359?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz" href="/user/show/14811808-liz">Liz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14811808-liz?shelf=headdesk-not-sorry">headdesk-not-sorry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14811808-liz?shelf=anticipated-2015">anticipated-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14811808-liz?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer856701359" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14555274310017769687"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415773309ra/11844025.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>Why? Tell me, why do authors do that? <br/>The conclusion could have been splendid, the author could have done something extra-ordinary, but no, what did she do instead? <br/>Focused on Alyssa's boy-problem. <br/><br/><i>Why my rating is so low (minor spoilers ahead) </i><br/><b>1.</b> The lack of character-development. Because yes, even in the final book there should be one, I think. What I got instead was Alyssa struggling with her feelings for the boys because her heart "tugged her in both ways", what I got instead was Jeb and hi</span>
  <span id="freeText14555274310017769687" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415773309ra/11844025.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Why? Tell me, why do authors do that? <br>The conclusion could have been splendid, the author could have done something extra-ordinary, but no, what did she do instead? <br>Focused on Alyssa's boy-problem. <br><br><i>Why my rating is so low (minor spoilers ahead) </i><br><b>1.</b> The lack of character-development. Because yes, even in the final book there should be one, I think. What I got instead was Alyssa struggling with her feelings for the boys because her heart "tugged her in both ways", what I got instead was Jeb and his "everything is my fault" attitude that I have already read about in both the first and the second book, what I got instead were poorly executed secondary characters, like Alyssa's dad.<br>Alyssa was not only not a queen, she was a hesitating weakling, in every possible sense, totally indecisive and whiny. <br>The only character who developed, at least a bit, was Morpheus, but I had expected that to be honest. In this one he was the only round and well-executed character who appeared to be in his place, unlike the others. <br><br><b>2.</b> Lack of plot, or plot being too slow for the final book. Again, the reason was the author's focus on the love-triangle and Alyssa's indecisiveness. Thanks to that she did nothing in this book. There were endless, "emotional" dialogues between her and one of the boys, there was her anxiety and fear about hurting either of them, but no freaking plot. <br>In she end all the work was done by Morpheus, Alyssa reminded me on a paperdoll she had compared herself with. <br>I had expected at least some kind of battle, but not a poorly described resolution where Alyssa did next to nothing and let the boys figure it out. The first 70% of the book there was Alyssa claiming how she would defeat Red and what happened? As aforementioned - <b>nothing.</b><br><br><b>3.</b> World-building? AnyElsewhere was something I wanted to be described. Instead, thanks to Alyssa letting everyone dictate her what to do and barely leaving one of the places at all I got next to nothing about the world. And it's a pity because I am sure if the author had chosen a different focus the book would have been amazing. In this one there was too little world-building. Some short descriptions here and there, one or two sentences in between Alyssa's whining and then a bit in the end. Oh, and just so you know, there was next to no Wonderland in this book too. Whole parts, which I think should have been discussed were just left out because the love triangle was more important. Right? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1393434246ra/8711181.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>4.</b> The love-triangle. Basically, the author decided to go the easy way. The resolution was so...shallow. And despite the fact that I should be pleased, the way everything was executed left nothing but a sour aftertaste. <br><br>There was no depth in this book. None. Sorry, I am not sorry at all.<br>Alyssa was a horrible MC, a typical damsel in distress, not that I have a problem with them, sometimes such characters are very interesting, but in her case it was annoying. <br>The resolution was...too simple, too easy, too short. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1411768679ra/11270879.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="14555274310017769687" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1060641830" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1060641830" />
    <a title="shady boots" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4972138-shady-boots"><img alt="shady boots" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592459241p2/4972138.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1060641830?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="shady boots" class="user" itemprop="url" name="shady boots" href="/user/show/4972138-shady-boots">shady boots</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=covergasm">covergasm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=meh-it-was-okay">meh-it-was-okay</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1060641830" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2996126901916015145">Well. Umm....<br/><br/>Okay, let's-- .... Hmm. This is gonna be the lengthiest review I've written in a loooooong time.<br/><br/>Man, you guys should see me right now. The top of my head is probably churning out smoke at this very moment due to me trying so hard to find the right words to say. Because in all honesty, I just do not know how I really feel about how this series wrapped up.<br/><br/>I guess judging from the rating you guys can already tell that I wasn't as happy as I'd hoped to be with it, considering I gave bot</span>
  <span id="freeText2996126901916015145" style="display:none">Well. Umm....<br /><br />Okay, let's-- .... Hmm. This is gonna be the lengthiest review I've written in a loooooong time.<br /><br />Man, you guys should see me right now. The top of my head is probably churning out smoke at this very moment due to me trying so hard to find the right words to say. Because in all honesty, I just do not know how I really feel about how this series wrapped up.<br /><br />I guess judging from the rating you guys can already tell that I wasn't as happy as I'd hoped to be with it, considering I gave both of the previous books 5 glowing stars. I was so excited for this book, and I really really wanted something epic, something life-changing, something that messed with my feels, even. But the story just got a little more convoluted and hard to follow for me, the third act was waaay too anti-climactic, and the love triangle became a bit too much to handle.<br /><br />It's hard for me to figure out if Alyssa is selfish in that she wants both guys for herself, or she's self<i>less</i> because she wants to make both of them happy. Perhaps it's a combination of the two, I dunno. But I just couldn't help myself from cringing every time Alyssa had intimate moments with one of them, only to have another one with the other a few chapters later. It just felt <i>wrong</i>.<br /><br />I'm just never comfortable with love triangles where the girl actually <i>loves</i> both of the guys. Usually there's always one guy that's clearly going to be the obvious choice. I'd thought that that was going to be the case; that Jeb was the good guy and Morph was the asshole. But each guy ended up having pros and cons of their own, and they eventually even got <i>me</i> being all indecisive. I didn't fall in love with either of them, of course, but I also couldn't figure out which guy I liked better than the other. I'm pretty sure the author intended this, though; to make the choice really really difficult.<br /><br />So was I surprised when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[there ended up being <i>no</i> choosing and Alyssa got to be with both of them in the end <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>? No. I kind of knew that was going to be the outcome, deep down. It just personally unsettled me, the whole thing. I don't know what it is exactly, but I felt uncomfortable during the entire last chapter and epilogue. <i>Really</i> uncomfortable.<br /><br />That's not to say I didn't enjoy the book. I did like that, in this series, both Alyssa's parents got their own stories fleshed out. While <i>Unhinged</i> gave us info about her mother, <i>Ensnared</i> explores the history of her father even more, and they each have a part to play in the story, which is a really great thing in YA, because parents are usually just cardboard cut-outs in the background, or some force of authority that the main character hates. I liked their overall inclusion. And of course, to write an <i>Alice</i> retelling you have to have an insane amount of imagination in your noggin, and I must say that A.G. Howard has just that, and then some. The imagery and overall aesthetic of this entire world she's created was wonderfully twisted and out of the box, as an <i>Alice</i> adaptation should be.<br /><br />Still, that doesn't change the fact that this series <i>does</i> focus on the love interests a little too much, and Alyssa's indecisiveness on who she should pick, because each guy held a part of her heart. The romance seemed to have too much weight to it, to the point where it was pretty much 80% of the story. I needed more than that. I wanted to be more connected to Alyssa, as a character, but all she concerned herself with was which guy to choose a lot of the time. It got me to once again question if all she cared about was her love life or if she really and truly cared for the well-being of Wonderland. I can't tell if she's selfish or selfless.<br /><br />So.... yeah, I can't think of anything else to say. Sure, I'm disappointed that the series didn't end the way I wished it did, but welp. No, actually, scratch that; I didn't really <i>wish</i> that the series would end in any particular way. I guess I was just hoping that it wouldn't have been the finale I ended up getting. Regardless, I'm sure the ending will be pleasing to a lot of the fans who have their panties catch fire over Jeb and Morpheus. But to me, that's the whole problem, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[that the author decided to try pleasing everyone. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I dunno, you guys. :/ I'm still stumped. Maybe some of you can share your opinions too, help me get a better grasp on this? I just feel all <i>weird</i> finishing this. I can't explain it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2996126901916015145" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_797762568" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/797762568" />
    <a title="Nereyda (Nick &amp; Nereyda&#39;s Infinite Booklist)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5383215-nereyda-nick-nereyda-s-infinite-booklist"><img alt="Nereyda (Nick &amp; Nereyda&#39;s Infinite Booklist)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1445582024p2/5383215.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/797762568?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nereyda (Nick &amp; Nereyda&#39;s Infinite Booklist)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nereyda (Nick &amp; Nereyda&#39;s Infinite Booklist)" href="/user/show/5383215-nereyda-nick-nereyda-s-infinite-booklist">Nereyda (Nick &amp; Nereyda&#39;s Infinite Booklist)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5383215-nereyda-nick-nereyda-s-infinite-booklist?shelf=what-a-let-down">what-a-let-down</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5383215-nereyda-nick-nereyda-s-infinite-booklist?shelf=book-looks">book-looks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer797762568" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18131343604705095756"><b>*SPOILERS WILL BE HIDDEN*</b> I was… pissed when I finished listening to the audiobook of this last week. I vented and ranted to a few of my friends hoping that would make me feel better, but even now, every time I think of this book I get in a bad mood. I really liked books one and two and I was so excited, and nervous for the final book. Final books are always scary. Final books involving a trilogy? Terrifying! Knowing that there is a good chance your Team might not win at the end? Devastating! I </span>
  <span id="freeText18131343604705095756" style="display:none"><b>*SPOILERS WILL BE HIDDEN*</b> I was… pissed when I finished listening to the audiobook of this last week. I vented and ranted to a few of my friends hoping that would make me feel better, but even now, every time I think of this book I get in a bad mood. I really liked books one and two and I was so excited, and nervous for the final book. Final books are always scary. Final books involving a trilogy? Terrifying! Knowing that there is a good chance your Team might not win at the end? Devastating! I know what you must be thinking. I’ve always been Team Jeb, so if I hated the ending then Morpheus must have won. But no, that’s not it at all! I kind of wish it were as simple as that…<br><br>I was annoyed by this story as a whole, not just the ending. We have the love triangle, which of course means that some back and forth between the MC and the two guys competing for her heart is expected. I was not a fan of the way this was pulled off in this case. I understand being indecisive. I understand being attracted to both Jeb and Morpheus. Hell, I understand that she might have feelings for both guys (although I don’t believe that you can truly love two people. Feelings, yes. Love, no) But we have the same back and forth with Alyssa and Jeb and Morpheus that we had in the last book. She loves Jeb, yada yada. But she has a past with Morpheus, yada yada. She wants to be with Jeb, yada yada. But she also wants to be with Morpheus, yada yada. But how can she betray Wonderland? How can she betray the prophecy that will save Wonderland?<br><br>The world, like always, is pretty freaking awesome! It’s so vivid and imaginative and I really would love to see pictures or sketches or something of just exactly what the author had in mind. We aren’t in Wonderland anymore, so things are a bit different and darker than they were the last time around. Jeb is… different (not bad different). Morpheus is still pretty much the same ol’ guy that he’s been in the last books. I really can’t say much more without giving out big spoilers, but the world is still as fantastic as it was in the previous books. Too bad it was boggled down by Alyssa’s dilemma: Jeb or Morpheus? The human world or Wonderland?<br><br><b>*MAJOR SPOILERS AND RANTING AHEAD! DON’T CLICK UNLESS YOU WANT TO KNOW WHAT HAPPENS AT THE END/WHO SHE ENDS UP WITH*</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I’m really not a fan (at all!) of how a love triangle in books is basically a free pass for the MC to mess around with two guys feelings. I’m especially not a fan when the MC kisses one guy while she’s with the other guy, but it’s supposed to be okay because it’s a love triangle. Or it’s supposed to be okay because she has history with the other guy. Alyssa got on my nerves so bad in this book! When she and Jeb find a way to forgive each other and work things out, she agrees to marry him and spend the rest of her life with him. But later on, while she is still engaged to Jeb, she lets Morpheus kiss her (more than just a simple or quick kiss). WTF! She doesn’t even try to push him away or anything. And when she tells him that she is marrying Jeb, he still doesn’t care (or her because she lets him). Alyssa ends up telling both guys that she loves them both and wants to be with both of them. And they are okay with it! You know, because they love her so much. Who would ever be okay with this in real life (except swingers)??? Their solution? Alyssa spends her human life with Jeb. They get married, have kids, grow old together and live a long and happy life. When he dies, she goes back to Wonderland. Morpheus of course, gives her ‘time to grieve’ before turning her back to her 17-year-old self and they live the rest of their immortal lives in Wonderland and end up saving it with their prophecy child. Sorry, but that is such a fucking cop-out! I’m not anti-love triangle, but I do want them to be executed right (they rarely are). If you’re gonna write a love triangle, you have to expect that one side of your readers won’t be happy with who the MC ends up with. Please don’t try to please both sides by somehow trying to find a bullshit loop-hole that technically allows both sides to be happy. It’s insulting to us readers and is basically the equivalent of giving a baby a pacifier. Honestly, I would have preferred if Alyssa would have just decided she loved Morpheus more and ended up staying with him. I would have been sad for Jeb, but oh well. Sometimes your Team just doesn’t win at the end. So yeah, that’s not even close to all the rants I had with this book, but I’ll just leave it at that. If you’re Team Morpheus, who will probably still like this book, because she ends up with him at the end. If you’re Team Jeb, you might like it because she technically picked him to spend her (human) life. Or you could just be annoyed like me by the cop-out ending… <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Don’t let my rating/review scare you off. You could very well still end up loving this book, doesn’t really matter if you are Team Jeb or Team Morpheus. I just couldn’t get over my disappointment of the story or Alyssa to find it in me to care…<br><br><b>Audiobook Comments:</b> It’s a shame that I hated the book because Rebecca Gibel is truly fantastic! I’ve listened to the previous books on audio (also narrated by her) and knew this was the only way for me to end the series. I can’t imagine anyone else narrating these books at the level of perfection that Gibel reached. Every single minor character has its own unique voice. I love when I can already tell which character is talking, just by the different tone the narrator uses. I love her Jeb voice, she nailed Morpheus’s voice and the Wonderland creatures were truly creepy. A fabulous performance!<br><br>***<br><b>Read full review &amp; more of my reviews at <a href="http://www.mostlyyabookobsessed.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Mostly YA Book Obsessed</a></b><br><a href="http://s1064.photobucket.com/albums/u367/nereyda1003/?action=view&amp;current=MyBlogSignature.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380349417i/703417.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Follow me at:</b><br><b>
  <a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/4471629" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin</a>

    <a title="Melissa (Ever So Mela)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28640648-melissa-ever-so-mela"><img alt="Melissa (Ever So Mela)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487543962p2/28640648.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa (Ever So Mela)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa (Ever So Mela)" href="/user/show/28640648-melissa-ever-so-mela">Melissa (Ever So Mela)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>
